Source pages p. 1071

Commentary
This passage consists of two indices from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa. The first is a subject index (fihris hijai lil-mabahith wa al-masail) listing key fiqh topics with page references. The second is a biographical index (fihris al-a'lam) of important personalities mentioned in the book. These indices are essential tools for navigating a comprehensive work on Islamic jurisprudence. They illustrate the systematic organization of Hanafi scholarship, where both theoretical rules (like the maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt') and historical figures (like the founding imams) are catalogued for quick reference. The inclusion of the qawida 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (certainty is not removed by doubt) as an entry highlights its central importance in Hanafi legal theory. Similarly, the biographical entry for Abu Yusuf mentions his famous statement from al-Kharaj about the sanctity of property. Such indices reflect the scholarly rigor and pedagogical structure of the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
اليقين لا يزول بالشك (al-yaqin la yuzalu bi al-shakk): A cardinal legal maxim meaning that a state of certainty is not overturned by mere doubt. It is listed as an index entry referencing page 6/81 of the book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The indices in Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm are indispensable for locating both subject discussions and the views of key Hanafi scholars.

Introduction and Front Matter

Bibliography of Key References in Hanafi Fiqh and Usul
Listing of primary and secondary references used in the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize the major references in hadith, usul al-fiqh, and Hanafi fiqh as listed by Mustafa al-Zarqa, and explain the significance of each category for a Mufti's training.

Core Idea
Knowing the foundational references is essential for a Mufti to issue correct rulings.

This passage from Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa's 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm' is a carefully curated bibliography of the most important sources for a Hanafi jurist. It is divided into three sections: hadith works, usul al-fiqh works, and Hanafi fiqh works. Each entry includes the author's name and death date, reflecting the scholarly rigor expected of a mufti. Understanding this list will help you navigate the Hanafi tradition and locate authoritative rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The bibliography is divided into hadith, usul al-fiqh, and Hanafi fiqh. Note the page layout: numbers 16-22 for hadith, 23-39 for usul, and 40-59 for fiqh.
Some numbers may be misprinted (e.g., 'YA' for 38, 'EA' for 48).
2
Recognize key authors and their madhhab affiliation
For each book, note the author and whether he is Hanafi (e.g., al-Bazdawi, al-Kasani) or from another school (e.g., Malik, al-Shafi'i via al-Ghazali). This helps in understanding the range of sources a Hanafi mufti uses.
Usul works include both Hanafi and Shafi'i/Maliki authors.
3
Understand the hierarchy of fiqh references
In the fiqh section, note the major texts like Bada'i' al-Sana'i', al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar with its commentary Radd al-Muhtar. These are foundational for fatwa.
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar is a matn (text) and Radd al-Muhtar is a hashiah (gloss) that often becomes the relied-upon position.
4
Link references to daily mufti practice
A mufti must consult these works: hadith for proof, usul for methodology, and fiqh for established rulings. This bibliography is a roadmap for study and research.

Source pages p. 1076

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (ثبت بأهم المراجع) in which the author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, lists the key primary and secondary sources used in his work 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm'. The list is divided into three sections: first, hadith works (e.g., the four Sunan, Muwatta, Riyad al-Salihin); second, usul al-fiqh works (e.g., Usul al-Bazdawi, al-Tahrir, al-Mustasfa); and third, Hanafi fiqh works (e.g., Bada'i' al-Sana'i', al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Durr al-Mukhtar). Many of these references are standard in Hanafi curricula. The author provides authors' death dates and occasionally the edition, indicating meticulous scholarly practice. This list serves as a guide for students to familiarize themselves with the foundational texts of the Hanafi madhhab and Islamic legal theory.

Key Terms
ثبت بأهم المراجع (Thabt bi-ahamm al-maraji'): List of the most important references used in the book.
السنن الأربعة (al-Sunan al-Arba'ah): The four Sunan collections: Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i.
أصول الفقه (Usul al-Fiqh): Principles of Islamic jurisprudence; the methodology for deriving rulings from sources.
الدر المختار (al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A famous Hanafi fiqh matn by al-Haskafi, often relied upon for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work listed in the bibliography?
A) Al-Muwatta'
B) Al-Mustasfa
C) Usul al-Bazdawi
D) Sunan Ibn Majah

Key Takeaway
The bibliography in Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm provides a curated list of essential references that every Hanafi mufti should know.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Hanafi Reference Hierarchy and the Mufti's Library
Bibliography of primary references

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi reference works and their place in the fatwa hierarchy, distinguishing between Zahir al-Riwaya, later commentaries, and codifications.

Core Idea
The mufti's authority flows from layered sources: core (Zahir al-Riwaya), extended (commentaries), operative (mufta bihi codifications).

This bibliography introduces the foundational texts that every Hanafi jurist and mufti must know. From al-Mabsut (the source) to al-Hidaya (the reference) to the Majalla (the code), each work occupies a specific rung in the hierarchy of fatwa. Recognizing these layers is essential for proper istidlal and tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify Zahir al-Riwaya works
Look for works that belong to the core six of Imam Muhammad. The list includes al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi, which is a primary Zahir al-Riwaya text. Recognize that al-Hidaya is a later distillation that often reflects the mufta bihi.
Zahir al-Riwaya texts are the most authoritative according to the school's hierarchy.
2
Locate the commentary tradition
Note the three commentaries on al-Hidaya: al-'Inaya, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Kifaya. These are essential for understanding ikhtilaf and tarjih within the school. A mufti frequently consults these to see the reasoning behind the preferred view.
Later commentaries may override some aspects of the base text when they rely on stronger proofs.
3
Recognize the codification layer
The Majalla is a state-enacted code that codifies the mufta bihi views. Its commentaries (e.g., Mir'at al-Majalla) are operational for fatwa in the Ottoman/post-Ottoman context. This layer simplifies access for the mufti.
The Majalla does not cover all fiqh areas; it focuses on mu'amalat.
4
Note cross-madhhab sources
The list includes works from Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali, and Zaydi schools. A mufti needs comparative knowledge to understand concepts like al-Fiqh 'ala al-Madhahib al-Arba'a and to address naqid cases.
Cross-madhhab works help in areas of overlap or when the Hanafi position is not widely accepted.
5
Identify works on qawa'id and fatawa
Look for texts like al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, Anwar al-Buruq, and Fatawa Ibn Taymiyya. These are tools for usul al-iftaa, providing maxims and precedents for novel issues.
Qawa'id works help the mufti derive consistent rulings across different chapters.

List of the Most Important References
62 - Al-Fara'id al-Bahiyya fi al-Qawa'id wa al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyya - by Shaykh Mahmud al-Hamzawi.
63 - Al-Qawl al-Hasan fi Jawab al-Qawl liman? - by 'Ata' Allah ibn Nu'ay (1038 AH). Lithographic print 1276 AH.
65 - Al-Mabsut - by Shams al-A'imma Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi (483 AH).
66 - Majami' al-Haqa'iq - by Muhammad Abu Sa'id al-Khadimi.
67 - Majallat al-Ahkam al-Shar'iyya (which is the Islamic civil code of the Ottoman Empire).
68 - Mir'at al-Majalla - by the jurist Mas'ud Afandi, Mufti of Kayseri.
69 - Sharh al-Majalla - by 'Allama Shaykh Khalid al-Atasi.
70 - Sharh al-Majalla - by Ustadh Salim Rustam al-Baz (1338 AH).
71 - Sharh al-Majalla - by 'Allama 'Ali Haydar (Arabicization by Ustadh Fahmi al-Husayni).
72 - Murshid al-Hayran - by 'Allama jurist Muhammad Qadri Basha al-Misri (1306 AH).
73 - Mu'in al-Hukkam - by 'Ala' al-Din 'Ali ibn Khalil al-Tarabulsi (844 AH).
74 - Al-Hidaya - by Burhan al-Din 'Ali al-Marghinani (593 AH). Maymaniyya edition year 1319 AH, which includes the following commentaries:
75 - Al-'Inaya Sharh al-Hidaya - by Akmal al-Din Muhammad al-Babarti (786 AH).
76 - Fath al-Qadir Sharh al-Hidaya - by Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam (861 AH) and its supplement.
77 - Al-Kifaya Sharh al-Hidaya - by Jalal al-Din al-Khwarazmi al-Karlani.
78 - Al-Ahkam al-Sultaniyya - by Abu al-Hasan 'Ali al-Mawardi al-Shafi'i (454 AH).
79 - Al-Ihkam fi Tamyiz al-Fatawa 'an al-Ahkam - by Shihab al-Din Ahmad al-Qarafi al-Maliki (684 AH).
80 - Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir - by Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti al-Shafi'i (911 AH), printed in Mecca.
81 - I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in - by Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya (751 AH).
82 - Al-Umm fi Madhhab al-Shafi'i - by Imam al-Shafi'i (204 AH).
83 - Al-Insaf - by 'Ala' al-Din 'Ali ibn Sulayman al-Maqdisi al-Hanbali (manuscript).
84 - Anwar al-Buruq fi al-Furuq (or Kitab al-Furuq) - by Shihab al-Din al-Qarafi al-Maliki (684 AH), printed by Dar Ihya' al-Kutub al-'Arabiyya in Cairo year 1347 AH, with its gloss Idrar al-Shuruq by al-Qasim ibn 'Abd Allah known as Ibn al-Shatt (723 AH) and its revision called Tahdhib al-Furuq by Muhammad 'Ali ibn Husayn al-Makki al-Maliki.
85 - Bidayat al-Mujtahid - by Qadi Abu al-Walid Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Rushd al-Hafid (595 AH), Jamaliyya print in Cairo year 1329 AH.
86 - Tabsirat al-Hukkam - by Burhan al-Din Ibrahim known as Ibn Farhun al-Ya'mari al-Maliki (799 AH).
87 - Durrat al-Ghawwas fi Muhadarat al-Khawwas - by Ibn Farhun al-Maliki, edited and annotated by Dr. Muhammad Abu al-Ajfan and 'Uthman Batikh, Cairo, Dar al-Turath 1980.
88 - Risala fi al-Ahliyya wa 'Awaridiha wa al-Wilaya - by the late 'Allama Shaykh Ahmad Ibrahim, professor of Shari'a at the Faculty of Law, Cairo University (1364 AH).
89 - Risala fi al-'Uqud wa al-Shurut - by the late 'Allama Shaykh Ahmad Ibrahim as well.
90 - Al-Siyasa al-Shar'iyya - by Ustadh Shaykh 'Abd al-Wahhab al-Khallaf, professor of Shari'a at the Faculty of Law, Cairo University.
91 - Al-Shafi Sharh al-Muqni' (or al-Sharh al-Kabir) - by Shams al-Din 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad known as Ibn Qudama al-Maqdisi (682 AH), printed with al-Mughni by al-Manar Press.
92 - Sharh al-Azhar fi Fiqh al-Shi'a al-Zaydiyya.
93 - Sharh al-Manhuma al-Rahbiyya fi al-Fara'id 'ala al-Madhhab al-Shafi'i by Muhammad Ahmad al-Sibt al-Mardini (809 AH).
94 - Al-Shari'a al-Islamiyya wa Huquq al-Usra fiha - by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, within the book Al-Thaqafa al-Islamiyya wa al-Hayat al-Mu'asira edited by Ustadh Muhammad Khalf Allah, Franklin Foundation, Cairo-New York, second edition 1962 CE.
95 - Fatawa Shaykh al-Islam Taqi al-Din Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad known as Ibn Taymiyya (728 AH).
96 - Al-Furu' - by Muhammad ibn Mufleh al-Hanbali, with its gloss Tashih al-Furu' by 'Ali al-Maqdisi, al-Manar print.
97 - Al-Fiqh 'ala al-Madhahib al-Arba'a - by al-Jaziri (1360 AH).
98 - Qa'idat al-'Uqud - by Ibn Taymiyya (manuscript), then recently printed in Egypt under the name Nazariyyat al-'Aqd.
99 - Al-Qawa'id - by 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Rajab al-Hanbali (795 AH).
100 - Qawa'id al-Ahkam - by 'Izz al-Din 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Abd al-Salam al-Shafi'i (660 AH).
101 - Al-Kafi fi Fiqh Ahl al-Madina - by Ibn 'Abd al-Barr al-Namari al-Qurtubi (463 AH), Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyya, Beirut.
Source pages p. 1078

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (ثبت بأهم المراجع) listing the primary references consulted by the author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, in his work 'al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Am'. The list is organized by fiqh school and includes foundational Hanafi works such as al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi, a cornerstone of Zahir al-Riwaya, and al-Hidaya by al-Marghinani, along with its major commentaries (al-'Inaya, Fath al-Qadir, al-Kifaya). Also noted are later Ottoman-era codifications like the Majalla and its commentaries. The bibliography extends to other madhhabs: Shafi'i works like al-Umm and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, Maliki works like al-Furuq by al-Qarafi, Hanbali works like al-Furu' by Ibn Muflih, and comparative fiqh works such as al-Fiqh 'ala al-Madhahib al-Arba'a. This list demonstrates the author's comprehensive approach, drawing on both classical and modern sources across schools, as well as works on qawa'id (legal maxims) and fatwa methodology. The inclusion of works by al-Zarqa himself (e.g., entry 94) shows his own contributions. This section is purely informational, providing the reader with the scholarly foundation of the book.

Key Terms
زاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwaya): The six authentic books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the core authority of the Hanafi school.
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): A foundational Hanafi work by al-Sarakhsi, part of Zahir al-Riwaya, containing detailed transmission of rulings.
الهداية (al-Hidaya): A concise Hanafi fiqh text by al-Marghinani, widely used for fatwa due to its tarjih choices.
مجلة الأحكام الشرعية (Majallat al-Ahkam al-Shar'iyya): The Ottoman codification of Hanafi mu'amalat law, composed of 1851 articles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following works is classified as a Zahir al-Riwaya text according to the bibliography?
A) الهداية
B) فتح القدير
C) المبسوط
D) المجلة

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy progresses from Zahir al-Riwaya (e.g., al-Mabsut) through later commentaries (e.g., al-Hidaya) to codifications (e.g., al-Majalla), and a mufti must navigate these layers skillfully to issue sound fatwas.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm: A Roadmap to Hanafi Fiqh Methodology
Table of contents summarizing the work's structure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the four main chapters of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm and identify which sections are most relevant to understanding Hanafi usul al-fiqh and iftaa methodology.

Core Idea
Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm is the essential map of the Hanafi jurist's intellectual journey — from sources to history to modern application.

This lesson introduces the table of contents of Mustafa al-Zarqa's seminal work, al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm. While a table of contents may seem straightforward, it reveals the author's deliberate pedagogical structure: first grounding the reader in the nature of Sharia and fiqh, then exploring the sources (including secondary ones like istihsan and istislah), then tracing the historical development of fiqh through eight stages, and finally addressing how classical fiqh can inform modern codification. As a Hanafi mufti-in-training, understanding this architecture will help you locate the relevant discussions for your own ijtihad and fatwa drafting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's bipartite structure
Note that the index covers two parts (juz'an). The first part contains the bulk of the material (chapters 1-4), while the second part is not detailed in this index but is referenced at the end.
The page number 1154 at the end of the Arabic indicates the total pages of the work.
2
Break down Part One into its four chapters
Part One has four chapters: 1) Introduction, definition, and classification; 2) Sources of Islamic fiqh; 3) Historical development of fiqh; 4) Deriving modern codification from fiqh. List them in order.
Each chapter groups related topics.
3
Analyze the subsections of each chapter
For Chapter Two (sources), note the distinction between primary (Section 3) and secondary sources (Sections 4-6: istihsan, istislah, 'urf). For Chapter Three (history), observe the eight chronological stages and the appendices on ijtihad of Umar, People of Hadith vs. Opinion, authority of ruler, and Majalla.
The appendices highlight key debates.
4
Relate the structure to a mufti's needs
Consider how a mufti would use this TOC to find rulings: e.g., for a modern issue, first consult sources (Chapter Two), then historical precedents (Chapter Three), then modern codification (Chapter Four).
This TOC serves as a navigation aid for fatwa research.

Brief index of topics of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm in its two parts (1). Part One: Chapter One: Introduction, Definition, and Division: Section 1: General overview of Islamic Sharia; Section 2: Meaning of fiqh and divisions of its rulings. Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Fiqh: Section 3: Primary sources of fiqh; Section 4: Secondary sources of fiqh: al-Istihsan; Section 5: Secondary sources of fiqh: al-Istislah; Appendix to Section 5: al-Siyasa al-Shar'iyya; Section 6: Secondary sources: al-Urf; Section 7: Ordering of sources of fiqh; Section 8: Difference between Sharia and fiqh. Chapter Three: Stages of Development of Islamic Fiqh and Their Characteristics: Section 9: Fiqh: its development and historical stages; Section 10: First stage: Prophetic era; Section 11: Second stage: Era of the Rightly Guided Caliphs; Appendix to Section 11: Ijtihad of Umar regarding lands; Section 12: Third stage: 50-100 AH (Appendix: People of Hadith and People of Opinion); Section 13: Fourth fiqh stage: 101-350 AH; Section 14: Fifth fiqh stage: 351-650 AH; Section 15: Sixth fiqh stage: 651-1286 AH; Appendix: Authority of the ruler; Section 16: Seventh fiqh stage: 1287-1354 AH; Appendix: Majallat al-Ahkam al-Adliyya; Section 17: Eighth fiqh stage: 1355 AH to present. Chapter Four: On Deriving Modern Codification from Islamic Fiqh: Section 18: Modern trend of benefiting from fiqh; Appendix: Examples. (1) (Detailed index at the end of the book - numbers of chapters and sections are indicated at the top of the pages). 1154
Source pages p. 1085

Commentary
This is the table of contents for the book, outlining its structure. The book is divided into parts, chapters, and sections. It covers introductory concepts, sources of fiqh (primary and secondary), historical development of Islamic jurisprudence, and finally the modern codification of Islamic law. Notable appendices include discussions on siyasa shar'iyya, Umar's ijtihad on land, the Majalla, and others. This index provides a roadmap for the reader. The detailed index is referenced at the end of the book.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): A secondary source of fiqh meaning juristic preference; departing from analogy for a stronger evidence.
الاستصلاح (al-istiṣlāḥ): A secondary source meaning public interest; consideration of benefit.
المجلة العدلية (al-Majalla al-ʿAdliyya): The Ottoman civil code codified Hanafi fiqh in the 19th century.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The index of al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm is a strategic map for any Hanafi mufti: it shows the progression from foundational concepts to sources, historical evolution, and modern codification.
